&& Sets

#### Easy

**1.** For any set A, the set A ‚à™ A is equal to:
A. A
B. ‚àÖ (the empty set)
C. U (the universal set)
D. A'
**Correct Answer: A**

**2.** The number of subsets of a set containing 4 elements is:
A. 4
B. 8
C. 16
D. 32
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** Which of the following is an empty set?
A. {x : x is an even prime number}
B. {x : x¬≤ = 4}
C. {x : x is a natural number and x < 1}
D. {x : x = x}
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** The set {x : x is a month of a year not having 31 days} is:
A. A finite set
B. An infinite set
C. An empty set
D. A singleton set
**Correct Answer: A**

**5.** For any set A, (A')' is equal to:
A. A
B. A'
C. ‚àÖ
D. U
**Correct Answer: A**

**6.** The representation of a set by listing all its elements is known as:
A. Set-builder form
B. Roster form
C. Interval form
D. Venn diagram
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** If A = {1, 2, 3} and B = {3, 4, 5}, then A ‚à© B is:
A. {3}
B. {1, 2, 3, 4, 5}
C. {1, 2}
D. {4, 5}
**Correct Answer: A**

**8.** The number of elements in the power set of a set with 'n' elements is:
A. n
B. 2n
C. n¬≤
D. 2‚Åø
**Correct Answer: D**

**9.** If A and B are disjoint sets, then n(A ‚à© B) is:
A. 1
B. 0
C. n(A)
D. n(B)
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** The set of all subsets of a given set A is called the:
A. Universal set of A
B. Complement of A
C. Power set of A
D. Union of A
**Correct Answer: C**

**11.** If A ‚äÇ B, then A ‚à™ B is equal to:
A. A
B. B
C. ‚àÖ
D. A ‚à© B
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** For any two sets A and B, A - B is the set of elements which are:
A. In A and B both

C. In B but not in A
D. In neither A nor B
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The set-builder form of the set {2, 4, 8, 16, 32} is:

B. {x : x = n¬≤, n ‚àà N and n ‚â§ 5}

**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** A set that contains only one element is called a:
A. Null set
B. Finite set
C. Unit set
D. Singleton set
**Correct Answer: D**

**15.** Which of the following is a finite set?
A. The set of all points on a line
B. The set of all natural numbers
C. The set of all letters in the English alphabet
D. The set of all circles passing through the origin
**Correct Answer: C**

**16.** De Morgan's law states that (A ‚à™ B)' is equal to:
A. A' ‚à™ B'
B. A' ‚à© B'
C. A ‚à© B
D. A ‚à™ B
**Correct Answer: B**

**17.** If A ‚äÇ B, then A ‚à© B is equal to:
A. A
B. B
C. A'
D. ‚àÖ
**Correct Answer: A**

**18.** The shaded region in the given Venn diagram represents:

A. A ‚à™ B
B. A ‚à© B
C. A - B
D. B
**Correct Answer: D**

**19.** A set that does not contain any element is called a(n):
A. Singleton set
B. Power set
C. Empty set
D. Infinite set
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** Two sets A and B are said to be equal if:

&& Sequence and Series

&& Straight Lines

Here are the question sets for Statistics and Probability, based on the KCET PYQ pattern and with the correct formatting.

&& Statistics

#### Easy

**1.** The measure of dispersion that is easiest to calculate is the:
A. Range
B. Variance
C. Standard Deviation
D. Mean Deviation
**Correct Answer: A**

**2.** The range of the data set: 2, 5, 9, 3, 12, 1, 15 is:
A. 15
B. 14
C. 13
D. 1
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** Variance is the square of the:
A. Mean
B. Range
C. Mean Deviation
D. Standard Deviation
**Correct Answer: D**

**4.** Which of the following is a measure of central tendency?
A. Range
B. Mean Deviation
C. Standard Deviation
D. Median
**Correct Answer: D**

**5.** The mean deviation is the average of the absolute deviations from a:
A. Central value (mean, median, or mode)
B. Maximum value
C. Minimum value
D. Quartile
**Correct Answer: A**

**6.** The standard deviation of a data set is always:
A. Negative
B. Zero
C. Non-negative
D. Less than the variance
**Correct Answer: C**

**7.** If the variance of a data set is 25, then its standard deviation is:
A. 5
B. 25
C. 625
D. 12.5
**Correct Answer: A**

**8.** The sum of the deviations of the items from their arithmetic mean is always:
A. 1
B. 0
C. A positive value
D. A negative value
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The measure of dispersion which is not affected by extreme values is:
A. Range
B. Quartile Deviation
C. Standard Deviation
D. Mean Deviation
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** The coefficient of variation is calculated as:
A. (Mean / Standard Deviation) √ó 100

C. (Range / Mean) √ó 100
D. (Mean / Range) √ó 100
**Correct Answer: B**

**11.** The mean of the first `n` natural numbers is:

**Correct Answer: B**

**Correct Answer: C**

D. Spread out
**Correct Answer: B**

B. 3
C. 3.5
D. 15
**Correct Answer: B**

A. Coefficient of variation

C. Range
D. Mean deviation
**Correct Answer: B**

A. Mean
B. Median
C. Mode
D. First term
**Correct Answer: B**

A. Central location
B. Spread or dispersion
C. Skewness
D. Correlation
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** The symbol œÉ is used to denote:
A. Variance
B. Mean
C. Standard Deviation
D. Coefficient of Variation
**Correct Answer: C**

A. Equal

D. Negative

&& Probability

&& Relations and Functions

#### Easy

**1.** A relation R on a set A is called reflexive if for every a ‚àà A:
A. (a, 1) ‚àà R
B. (1, a) ‚àà R
C. (a, a) ‚àà R
D. (a, b) ‚àà R implies (b, a) ‚àà R
**Correct Answer: C**

**2.** A function f : A ‚Üí B is said to be one-one (injective) if distinct elements of A have:
A. The same image in B
B. Different images in B
C. At least one image in B
D. No image in B
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** A function f : A ‚Üí B is said to be onto (surjective) if the range of f is equal to its:
A. Domain (A)
B. Codomain (B)
C. A subset of the domain

**Correct Answer: B**

**4.** A function which is both one-one and onto is called a:
A. Injective function
B. Surjective function
C. Bijective function
D. Constant function
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** Let A = {1, 2, 3}. Which of the following relations on A is reflexive?

C. (b, b) ‚àà R
D. (a, c) ‚àà R

&& Linear Programming

#### Easy

**1.** The region of a plane that represents the solution set of a system of linear inequalities is called the:
A. Optimal region
B. Feasible region
C. Objective region
D. Constraint region
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The linear function which is to be maximized or minimized in a linear programming problem (LPP) is called the:
A. Constraint
B. Feasible solution
C. Objective function
D. Optimal solution
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** In an LPP, the conditions or restrictions on the variables are called:
A. Objectives
B. Solutions
C. Constraints
D. Functions
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** Any point in the feasible region that gives the optimal value (maximum or minimum) of the objective function is called an:
A. Optimal solution
B. Feasible solution
C. Corner point
D. Infeasible solution
**Correct Answer: A**

**5.** The non-negative constraints for the variables x and y in an LPP are:
A. x > 0, y > 0
B. x ‚â§ 0, y ‚â§ 0
C. x = 0, y = 0
D. x ‚â• 0, y ‚â• 0
**Correct Answer: D**

**6.** The optimal value of the objective function in an LPP is attained at the:
A. Center of the feasible region
B. Corner points (vertices) of the feasible region
C. Any point inside the feasible region
D. Origin
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** A feasible region that can be enclosed within a circle is called a:
A. Bounded feasible region
B. Unbounded feasible region
C. Open feasible region
D. Closed feasible region
**Correct Answer: A**

**8.** If the feasible region for an LPP is empty, then the solution is:
A. Optimal
B. Feasible
C. Infeasible (no solution)
D. Unbounded
**Correct Answer: C**

**9.** The graphical method is used to solve LPPs with:
A. One variable
B. Two variables
C. Three variables
D. Any number of variables
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** A point that satisfies all the given constraints of an LPP is called a:
A. Feasible solution
B. Optimal solution
C. Corner point
D. Non-negative solution
**Correct Answer: A**

**11.** The first step in solving an LPP graphically is to:
A. Find the corner points
B. Identify the objective function
C. Formulate the problem mathematically
D. Plot the constraints to find the feasible region
**Correct Answer: D**

**12.** The objective of an LPP for a manufacturer is usually to:
A. Minimize cost
B. Maximize profit
C. Either A or B
D. Neither A nor B
**Correct Answer: C**

**13.** The inequality 2x + 3y ‚â§ 6 represents the region:
A. On the line 2x + 3y = 6
B. Containing the origin
C. Not containing the origin
D. In the first quadrant only
**Correct Answer: B**

**14.** The constraints of an LPP are always:
A. Linear equations
B. Linear inequalities
C. Quadratic equations
D. Quadratic inequalities
**Correct Answer: B**

**15.** A feasible region that extends indefinitely in any direction is called:
A. Bounded
B. Unbounded
C. Finite
D. Infinite
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The corner points of a feasible region are the points of:
A. Intersection of the boundary lines
B. The origin
C. The axes
D. The objective function
**Correct Answer: A**

**17.** The problem of finding the best or most effective way of using limited resources to achieve a certain objective is:
A. A quadratic problem
B. A calculus problem
C. A linear programming problem
D. A probability problem
**Correct Answer: C**

**18.** The inequality x ‚â• 0 represents the region to the:
A. Left of the y-axis
B. Right of the y-axis (including the y-axis)
C. Above the x-axis
D. Below the x-axis
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** An LPP has constraints of the type:
A. x ‚â• 0, y ‚â• 0
B. ax + by ‚â§ c or ax + by ‚â• c
C. Both A and B
D. Z = ax + by
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** The final step in the corner point method is to:
A. Find the feasible region

**48.** A firm manufactures two types of products A and B and sells them at a profit of ‚Çπ2 on type A and ‚Çπ3 on type B. The constraints are 3x + 2y ‚â§ 12, x + 5y ‚â§ 20, x, y ‚â• 0. The maximum profit is:
A. ‚Çπ12
B. ‚Çπ13.2
C. ‚Çπ15
D. ‚Çπ16.4
**Correct Answer: B**
*(Note: The optimal point is a fraction, (20/13, 36/13), which gives a profit of 152/13 ‚âà 11.69. Let me recheck the typical KCET problem constraints... usually they result in integer corner points. Let me re-verify the corner points: (0,0) Z=0; (4,0) Z=8; (0,4) Z=12; Intersection of 3x+2y=12 and x+5y=20 is (20/13, 36/13) Z = (20/13)*2 + (36/13)*3 = (40+108)/13 = 148/13 ‚âà 11.38. The max value is 12 at (0,4). Let's find a better KCET-style problem... A common pattern is having integer solutions. Let's adjust the profit function to Z = 3x+5y. Then at (0,4) Z=20, at (4,0) Z=12, at (20/13, 36/13) Z=60/13+180/13=240/13~18.46. The max is 20 at (0,4). Let's use that.*
**Let's rephrase the question for a cleaner answer.**
**48.** A firm manufactures two types of products A and B and sells them at a profit of ‚Çπ3 on type A and ‚Çπ5 on type B. The constraints are 3x + 2y ‚â§ 12, x + 5y ‚â§ 20, x, y ‚â• 0. The maximum profit is:
A. ‚Çπ12
B. ‚Çπ20
C. ‚Çπ18.46
D. ‚Çπ15
**Correct Answer: B**

&& Probability

D. P(B) / P(A), where P(A) ‚â† 0
**Correct Answer: A**

**10.** If A and B are independent events, then P(A ‚à© B) is equal to:
A. P(A) + P(B)
B. P(A) - P(B)
C. P(A) √ó P(B)
D. P(A) / P(B)
**Correct Answer: C**

**11.** A coin is tossed twice. The probability of getting exactly one head is:
A. 1/4
B. 1/2
C. 3/4
D. 1

C. Mathematical formula

**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The sum of the probabilities in a probability distribution is always:
A. 0
B. 1

D. Greater than 1

C. Simple trial
D. Compound trial

A. The probability of an event

D. The probability of a union of events
**Correct Answer: C**

**16.** The mean of a probability distribution is also known as its:
A. Variance
B. Standard Deviation
C. Expected Value
D. Median
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** In a binomial distribution B(n, p), 'n' represents the:

**18.** If P(A) = 1/2, P(B) = 0, then P(A|B) is:
A. 0
B. 1/2
C. Not defined
D. 1

**19.** Two events are independent if the occurrence of one:
